тАШ рдЕрдЬрд╛рддрд╢рддреНрд░реБрдореН’ рдЗрддрд┐ рдирд╡рд░реНрдЪрдВ рджреНрд╡рд┐рддреАрдпрдВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдЬрд╛рдкрддреНрдпрд╕реНрдп рд╕рдВрд╡рд░рдгрд╕реНрдпрд╛рд░реНрд╖рдореИрдиреНрджреНрд░рдореН ред рдирд╡рдореА рддреНрд░рд┐рд╖реНрдЯреБрдкреН рд╢рд┐рд╖реНрдЯрд╛рд╕реНрддреНрд░рд┐рд╖реНрдЯреБрдмрдиреНрддрдкрд░рд┐рднрд╛рд╖рдпрд╛ рдЬрдЧрддреНрдпрдГ ред тАШ рдЕрдЬрд╛рддрд╢рддреНрд░реБ рдирд╡ рддреНрд░рд┐рд╖реНрдЯреБрдмрдиреНрддрдореН’ рдЗрддреНрдпрдиреБрдХреНрд░рдордгрд┐рдХрд╛ ред рд╡рд┐рдирд┐рдпреЛрдЧреЛ рд▓реИрдЩреНрдЧрд┐рдХрдГ рее

Jamison Brereton

34 (388)
Indra
Saс╣Гvaraс╣Зa Pr─Бj─Бpatya
9 verses: jagat─л, except triс╣гс╣нubh 9
The first three verses of this hymn urge sacrificers to make offerings to Indra and promise them a return on this investment of ritual energy, and the preoccupation throughout most of the hymn is the contrast between the generous and the stingy and their respective fates (see esp. vss. 5тАУ7). There is a hostile and dangerous edge to

much of the rhetoric: the punishments Indra metes out to non-givers are described with gusto.
But the most curious feature of the hymn is verse 4, where Indra, depicted as the killer of the father, mother, and brother of an apparently blameless man, not only feels no remorse (тАЬhe does not shrink from his offenseтАЭ), but expects to receive offerings from his victim. The word тАЬoffenseтАЭ used here is a rare and charged one (k├нlbiс╣гa): the uncompounded form is found only here in the R╠еgveda, and the four other (compounded) occurrences of it are in late hymns in Maс╣Зс╕Нala X. Our passage here seems a foreshadowing of a theme in Indra mythology that becomes highly developed in the middle Vedic period, that of IndraтАЩs offenses or misdeeds, cata logued as a set of kilbiс╣г─Бс╣Зi (see Jamison 1991: 64тАУ68), with Indra as the figure of a warrior run amuck. But the theme seems out of place in the context here, save perhaps for IndraтАЩs excessively aggressive behavior toward the stingy in other verses. (The stingy deserve this treatment, however, in the ritual calculus of the R╠еgveda; the man violently deprived of his kin does not.)
The hymn ends with what appears to be a truncated d─Бnastuti (vs. 9): the poet praises his apparent patron ─Аgnive┼Ыi ┼Ъatri, but no gifts are mentioned.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Indra

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe undecaying, heaven-conferring, unlimited (sacrificial) food, goes to the tamer (of enemies), whose adversarie are unborn; therefore (priests) pour out (the libation), dress (the cakes and butter), diligently discharge (your offices) to him who is the accepter of prayer, who si glorified by many.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Autonomous power, unaging, solar, immeasurable, speeds after him, the wondrous, whose rival has not been born.
Press, cook for the one whose vehicle is the sacred formulation; set more (offerings) out for the one praised by many.

Jamison Brereton Notes

A personified (/divinized) form of Svadh─Б тАШautonomous powerтАЩ is found in this set of hymns; cf. the apparent ref. to her also in V.32.10.

Griffith

BOUNDLESS and wasting not, the heavenly food of Gods goes to the foeless One, doer of wondrous deeds.
Press out, make ready, offer gifts with special zeal to him whom many laud, accepter of the prayer.

Geldner

Dem Meister, der keinen ebenb├╝rtigen Gegner hat, folgt die alterlose himmlische unermessene Selbstherrlichkeit. Presset, kochet f├╝r ihn, den die erbauliche Rede anzieht. Dem Vielgepriesenen setzet recht viel vor!

Grassmann

Dem gegnerlosen strebt die eigne Sch├╢pfung nach die unermessne, ewige, dem herrlichen; Auf, presst und kochet dem, der gern Gebet empf├дngt, dem vielgepriesnen bringt noch gr├╢ssre Gaben dar.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMaghavan, who fills his belly with the Soma, to be exhilarated (by drinking) of the sweet-savoured beverage, whereupon he has lifted up his destructive thousand-edged weapon, desiring to slay (the asura) Mmс╣Ыga.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Thousand-edged: sahasra bhс╣Ыс╣гс╣нim = aparimita tejas, of unbounded lustre

Jamison Brereton

He who filled his belly with soma, the bounteous one, drew exhilaration from the honey, the stalk,
when U┼Ыan─Б, possessing the great weapon, held the thousand-spiked weapon (out to him), to smash the wild beast.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The overall structure of the vs. is the first issue to address. The first hemistich begins with a rel. clause (in a) with accented verb ├бpiprata; the second p─Бda begins with another accented verb, ├бmandata, which can owe its accent either to its p─Бda-initial position or to being part of the rel. cl. of p─Бda a. I choose the former interpr., making b into the main cl. of the vs. (so also Hoffmann, Injunk., 244). Geldner and Witzel Got┼Н choose the second, with ab containing two parallel rel. clauses. Since the 2nd hemistich consists of a dep. cl. beginning with y├бd in c, with its accented verb y├бmat in d, this leaves the vs. without a main cl. Witzel Got┼Н remedy this by providing a main cl.

frame тАЬZur Stelle (war er) тАжтАЭ This posited main clause consists entirely of the preverb ─Б╠Бthat begins p─Бda a (see their n.), a slender reed indeed. Offhand I cannot think of any other examples where a preverb by itself constitutes a clause. This interpr. is esp. unlikely because ─Б╠Бis an extremely common preverb with тИЪpс╣Ы / pr─Б тАШfillтАЩ, and its default interpr. here is as a preverb in tmesis with ├бpiprata.

This structural question is connected with the problem of y├бmat in the y├бd cl.

of the 2nd hemistich. This form should be a subjunctive to the root aor., but it is difficult to construe it as such, viewed in conjunction with the augmented imperfects of ab. In order to hold onto the subjunctive interpr., Hoffmann (Injunk., 244) takes cd as a purpose cl. (тАЬDer Freigebige тАж berauschte sich тАж. auf dass ihm тАж U┼Ыan─Б тАж die tausendspitzige Waffe reicheтАЭ), but Indra doesnтАЩt drink soma so that U┼Ыan─Б will give him a weapon, but does so at the same time and occasion when U┼Ыan─Б gives him the weapon (see, e.g., I.121.12). Witzel Got┼НтАЩs тАЬZur Stelle (war er)тАЭ is obviously designed to provide a better pragmatic foundation for the purpose cl. (see their n.), but I have just treated the weakness of their interpr. I therefore think that y├бmat here has to be a nonce injunction with preterital value, rather than the subjunctive it appears to be.

The pivotal form that allowed this reanalysis is 3rd pl. yaman. This form is morphologically ambiguous: it could be a subjunctive or an injunctive. Although those forms are normally differentiated by the grade of the root (e.g., subj. g├бman versus injunc. gm├бn), a zero-grade injunc. *im├бn is too radical and would be blocked.

In fact, yaman, which occurs 4x (once as a rep.), is only found in m─Б╠Бprohibitives and therefore must be an injunc. in every case. To this form, which could also be injunc.

to a thematic stem, a 3rd sg. thematic-type injunc. y├бmat can be backformed.

On them. ├бpiprata see Narten 1969 = Kl. Sch. 108-24, esp. 109, 121-24.

Griffith

When Usana, that he might slay the monstrous beast, gave him the mighty weapon with a thousand points.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬHe who pours out the libation to that Indra, by day or by night, undoubtely becomes illustrious; ┼Ъakra disregards tthe man who is proud of his descendants and vain of his person n, and who, though wealthy, is the friend of the base.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Proud of his descendants and vain of his person n: tatanuс╣гс╣нim tan┼л┼Ыubhram = he who desires, (vaс╣гс╣нi) an extended (tata) race (santatim) and he whose person n (tanu) is decorated (┼Ыubhra) with ornaments, and in both implying svapoс╣гakam ayajv─Бnam, a self-cherisher not offering sacrifice

Jamison Brereton

Whoever presses soma for him in the heat or whoever in the cold, he certainly becomes heaven-bright.
The able one, the bounteous one who is partner to the poet (/Kavi
[U┼Ыan─Б]), snatches off the extended (garment), resplendent on
his body.

Jamison Brereton Notes

On ┼л╠Бdhar / ┼л╠Бdhan- as тАШcoldтАЩ, beside the homonym тАШudderтАЩ, see comm. ad VIII.2.12. Note the phonological echo at the end of p─Бdas a and c: ┼л╠Бdhani# / ┼лhati#.

There is considerably more phonological play in the 2nd hemistich: tatan├║с╣гс╣нim ┼лhati, tan┼л╠Б┼Ыubhram, enclosed within unbroken a’s: ├бp─Бpa ┼Ыakr├б┼Ы … magh├бv─Б y├бс╕е kav─Бsakh├бс╕е. This phonological pattern may help account for some of the difficulties of interpr. this hemistich. Before addressing the three hapaxes in cd, tatan├║с╣гtim, tan┼л╠Б┼Ыubhram, and k├бv─Бsakhaс╕е, note that the ─Бmreс╕Нited preverb ├бpa-apa (that is, ├бp─Бpa) superficially reads as a stem тАШnot evilтАЩ. I doubt if that is accidental, esp. since doubled preverbs are quite rare; we will return to it below.

The first two of the hapaxes form the object of ├бpa тАж ┼лhati. The lexeme ├бpa тИЪ┼лh means тАШpull awayтАЩ. It is used of the extended penis in cosmic incest in X.61.5; more to the point, in AV XVIII.2.57 it is used of a garment that is to be removed (тАж v─Б╠Бsaс╕е тАж ├бpait├бd ┼лha y├бd ih─Б╠Бbibhaс╕е pur─Б╠Б). A garment could well be described as tan┼л╠Б┼Ыubhra- тАШresplendent on the bodyтАЩ; cf. I.85.3 tan┼л╠Бс╣гu ┼Ыubhr─Б╠Бс╕е of the MarutsтАЩ ornaments. I therefore supply тАШgarmentтАЩ as the obj. here. (For a possible variant of this see disc. below.) Geldner refuses to tr. or discuss tatan├║с╣гс╣нi-; AiG is entirely silent on it; Oldenberg is noncommittal. Nonetheless, the formation of tatan├║с╣гс╣нi- looks fairly transparent, if quite unprecedented. As Witzel Got┼Н also suggest, it appears to be a -ti- abstract built to the weak grade of the pf. part. to тИЪtan тАШstretchтАЩ. Witzel Got┼Н gloss тАШdie Sich-ausgebreitet-haben-schaftтАЩ, which in their interpr. is then also applicable to someone who has this quality. They thus assume a personal object for ├бpa ┼лhati, a dandy (Geck): тАЬden, der sich ausgebreitet hat тАж den Geck.тАЭ IтАЩm not sure what a тАЬsich ausgebreitetтАЭ person would be, and there are other reasons to prefer supplying тАШgarmentтАЩ or something similar as the referent of these two acc. First, there is the AV passage just cited, where тАШgarmentтАЩ is the obj. of ├бpa тИЪ┼лh. Second, garments are objects of тИЪtan elsewhere (I.115.4, 134.4; X.106.1). And third, a personal object requires the meaning of ├бpa тИЪ┼лh to be seriously attenuated (Witzel Got┼НтАЩs abschieben: тАШpush away, get rid ofтАЩ). I therefore take тАШspread-out-nessтАЩ to be a quality attributed to a garment or garmentlike object. However, this analysis causes problems of its own. For one thing, why not simply use the pf. part. alone to qualify the underlying тАШgarmentтАЩ? Forming a derivational monstrosity – a -ti-abstract based on a pf. part. – and then turning this stem into a possessive adj. seem a tremendous amount of bother to go to when the participle by itself would convey the sense. Further, the standard words for garment are neut. (v─Б╠Бsas-, v├бstra-), and tatan├║с╣гс╣нim must be masc. (see the adj. tan┼л╠Б┼Ыubhram agreeing with it). A proper neut. sg. adj. built to a -ti-stem should end in -ti (though as far as I can tell, there are no exx. in the RV), so if tatan├║с╣гс╣нim is an adj., it is in the wrong gender for the posited noun it modifies. On the other hand, if we try to take tatan├║с╣гс╣нim simply as the -ti-abstract, not an adj. based on it, the masc. gender of the qualifier tan┼л╠Б┼Ыubhram clashes, since -ti-abstracts are fem. I have only an ad hoc answer to these problems: assuming the form is an adj. whose underlying referent is neut., the bare neut. -ti ending may have seemed anomalous and a more orthodox looking acc. substituted for it, encouraged also by the fact that the next word begins with a vowel and an inserted -m would avoid the hiatus. Meter would be unaffected, and tan┼л╠Б┼Ыubhram can of course be neut. instead of masc. But I do not find this explanation compelling, and a different possibility is discussed below.

I have discussed the third hapax, kav─Бsakh├б-, in some detail in Fs. Jasanoff (2007: 163), reviving the old, but generally now rejected, analysis of the first member as the old nom. sg. of kav├н- matching the Aves. nom. sg. kauu─Б with its hysterokinetic inflection. That this inflectional type may be preserved here may be signalled by the 2nd member -sakh├бс╕е, whose inflection remains hysterokinetic in Vedic and whose nom. sg. is ordinarily s├бkh─Б. The current standard interpr. of kav─Бhere assigns it to a stem (*)kava- тАШhumiliating, degradingтАЩ (see EWA s.v. kavatn├║-).

So, e.g., GeldnerтАЩs rendering of the cmpd as тАШfalsch FreundтАЩ, with some semantic weakening.

How one analyses the cmpd. depends on what one thinks is going on in the hemistich in general. The first question is who is the referent of the cmpd.? It is found in a two-word nominal rel. cl. y├бс╕е kav─Бsakh├бс╕е. Both Geldner and Witzel Got┼Н take its antecendent to be the obj. of the verb ├бpa тАж ┼лhati (e.g., Witzel Got┼Н тАЬтАж den Keck, der die Genossen geringsch├дtztтАЭ), but as was just discussed, it is not at all certain (and in my opinion unlikely) that the object of that verb is a person. Moreover, word order – an often helpful, though of course not sturdily reliable guide in the RV – favors Indra as referent: the verse ends тАж magh├бv─Б y├бс╕е kav─Бsakh├бс╕е.

If my analysis is correct – that the cmpd. contains kav├н- тАШpoetтАЩ and that it characterizes Indra – how can I fit it together with the rest of the vs.? I think the cmpd. has a double sense. On the one hand, the kav─Б part refers to U┼Ыan─Б K─Бvya, who figures in vs. 2. In fact, note that in 2d u┼Ы├бn─Б appears in its usual position, immediately after the caesura following an opening of 5. If we superimpose 3d over 2d, kav─Б- would immediately follow u┼Ы├бn─Б: [x x x x x / u┼Ы├бn─Б kav─Б(-sakha)], the composite yielding a simulacrum of his full name. And of course, as vs. 2 shows, Indra and U┼Ыan─Б are partners and companions. U┼Ыan─Б is referred to as kav├нelsewhere, with kav├н- a substitute for his patronymic; see, e.g., IV.16.3, 26.1.

But the other sense I see here is more sinister and requires considering vs. 3 in connection with the flg. verse. Vs. 4 is a curious, counter-intuitive, and indeed dispiriting vs.: even if Indra kills all your relatives, he still expects you to continue to offer to him. The usual comforting notion in the RV – that Indra will do well by you if you do well by him, while the non-offerer will get badly treated – is overturned here. Indra can act cavalierly and arbitrarily to ruin your life no matter how devotedly you serve him. I think the same unsettling idea is presented in vs. 3.

Though the standard interpr. of vs. 3 (see, e.g., GeldnerтАЩs n. 3cd) is that the first hemistich depicts the pious man happily rewarded, while cd shows the impious one getting his just deserts, I take the whole vs. as referring to the ups and downs of the pious somapresser. First, his labors pay off: he becomes dyum─Б╠Бn тАШheaven-brightтАЩ. But in the second half Indra snatches away this brightness, which is spread across him like a garment, тАЬresplendent on his bodyтАЭ (tan┼л╠Б┼Ыubhra-), an appropriate characterization of such brightness. In this reading kav─Б┼Ыakh├бс╕е is ironic; Indra was indeed a companion and partner of the poet, until he wasnтАЩt.

If this interpr. is correct, it may help explain the use of the peculiar formation tatan├║с╣гс╣нi- discussed at length above. In p─Бda b the lucky soma-presser is dyu-m├бnt-, lit. тАШpossessing dyu-тАШ. And by my analysis, it is this purported dyu- that is resplendent on his body. But the well-attested possessive adj. dyu-m├бnt- has become lexically separated from div-/ dyu- тАШheavenтАЩ; there is no independent dyu- тАШbrightnessтАЩ that can become the property of a person. (The root noun dy├║t- is rare without preverb and means yet again something different.) It may be that тАЬspreading-nessтАЭ is an attempt to capture the quality of heavenly light without having a firm grammatical base, an identifiable independent noun, to found it on. One of the standard tropes using the root тИЪtan is light or a source of light spreading through heaven and other cosmic realms; cf., e.g., X.88.3 of S┼лrya y├│ bh─Бn├║n─Б pс╣Ыthiv─л╠Бс╣Г dy─Б╠Бс╣Г ut├йm─Б╠Бm, ─Бtat─Б╠Бna r├│das─л ant├бrikс╣гam. And so tatan├║с╣гс╣нi- may embody this whole complex of heavenly light spreading across the manтАЩs body as if through heaven. By this analysis the tatan├║с╣гс╣нiis not a garment, as I first suggested, but like a garment.

Another piece of evidence may support my view of cd as expressing the undeserved and capricious reversal of fortune of the soma-presser who was riding high in ab. Remember that cd begins with the double preverb ├бp─Бpa, which could also be the voc. of an adj. тАШnot-evilтАЩ. I suggest that this is a despairing address to the soma-presser of ab: тАЬo un-evil [/blameless] one, see what can happen to you anyway.тАЭ

Griffith

Illustrious is the man whoever presseth out Soma for him in sunshine or in cloud and rain.
The mighty Maghavan who is the sage’s Friend advanceth more and more his beauteous progeny.

Wer ihm bei Sonnenglut oder wer bei Nachtk├╝hle Soma pre├Яt, der wird f├╝rwahr glorreich. Der M├дchtige, Freigebige streift dem, der ein falscher Freund ist, den am Leibe gl├дnzenden …….. ganz ab.

Grassmann

Wer ihm in heitrer, oder wer in tr├╝ber Zeit den Soma keltert, der f├╝rwahr ist glanzerf├╝llt; Den Prahler st├╢sst zur├╝ck der starke, m├дchtige, den eitlen Stutzer, der dem Kargen sich gesellt.

Elizarenkova

рд╢рдХреНрд░рдГ рд╢рдХреНрддреЛрд╜рдпрдВ рдпрд╕реНрдп рдЕрдпрдЬреНрд╡рдирдГ рдкрд┐рддрд░рдВ рдЕрд╡рдзреАрддреН рд╣рддрд╡рд╛рдиреН ред рдпрд╕реНрдп рдЪ рдорд╛рддрд░рдореН рдЕрд╡рдзреАрддреН ред рдпрд╕реНрдп рдЪ рднреНрд░рд╛рддрд░рдВ рдЕрддрдГ рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рджрдпрдЬреНрд╡рдирдГ рд╕рдХрд╛рд╢рд╛рддреН рди рдИрд╖рддреЗ ред рди рдмрд┐рднреЗрддрд┐ рди рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрддрд┐ рд╡рд╛ ред рдХрд┐рдВрддреБ рдЕрд╕реНрдп рдкреНрд░рдпрддрд╛ рдкреНрд░рджрддреНрддрд╛рдирд┐ рд╣рд╡реАрдВрд╖рд┐ рд╡реЗрддреАрджреН рдХрд╛рдордпрдд рдПрд╡ ред рдЕрдпрдЬреНрд╡рд╛рдирдВ рд╢рд┐рдХреНрд╖рдпрд┐рддреНрд╡рд╛ рдирд┐рдпреЛрдЬрдпрддреАрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ ред рдпрддрдВрдХрд░: рдпрдордирдХрд░реНрддрд╛ рд╡рд╕реНрд╡рдГ рд╡рд╕реБрдирдГ рдзрдирд╕реНрдп рдЖрдХрд░рдГ рдЕрднрд┐рдореБрдЦреНрдпрдХрд░реНрддрд╛ рдпрдГ рдХрд┐рд▓реНрдмрд┐рд╖рд╛рддреН рдкрд┐рддреНрд░рд╛рджрд┐рд╡рдзрдпреБрдХреНрддрд╛рддреН рди рдИрд╖рддреЗ рди рдЪрд▓рддрд┐ рди рдмрд┐рднреЗрддрд┐ рд╡рд╛ ред рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╕реНрдп рдЕрд╕реНрддреЛрддреДрдгрд╛рдВ рд╣рддрд┐рдГ тАШрдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░реЛ рдпрддреАрдиреН рд╕рд╛рд▓рд╛рд╡реГрдХреЗрднреНрдпрдГ рдкреНрд░рдпрдЪреНрдЫрддреН рдЕрдиреНрддрд░рд┐рдХреНрд╖реЗ рдкреМрд▓реЛрдорд╛рдиреН рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдВ рдХрд╛рд▓рдХрд╛рдЮреНрдЬреНрдпрд╛рдирд░реБрдиреНрдореБрдЦрд╛рдиреНрдпрддреАрдиреН рд╕рд╛рд▓рд╛рд╡реГрдХреЗрднреНрдпрдГ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдпрдЪреНрдЫрдореН’ рдЗрддреНрдпрд╛рджрд┐рд╢реНрд░реБрддрд┐рд╖реБ рдкреНрд░рд╕рд┐рджреНрдзрд╛ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬ┼Ъakra does not turn away from him whose father, whose mother, whose brother he has slain, but is willing to accept his offerings; the regulator (of acts), the bestower of riches, does not turn away from iniquity.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Does not turn away: na ata ─лс╣гate = he does not fear, or does not go up or from hence, na bibheti na gacchati v─Б; whose brother he has slain: avadh─лt has the nominative native ┼Ыakra; in the second line kilviс╣г─Бd ─лс╣гate, he, Indra, does not go from sin, sin is a reference to the sinner, that is, from one who is a patricide or the like, pitr─Бdi vadha yukt─Бt, that is, he does not turn away from who has committed these crimes; the reason is: veti idvasya prayata, for verily he desires his offerings, prayat─Бni dad─Бni

Jamison Brereton

The man whose father the able one has smashed, whose mother, whose brotherтАФhe [=Indra] does not shrink (even) from him.
Rather, he actually pursues his offerings; the arranger, the distributor of goods does not shrink from his offense.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As noted in the published introduction. and in the disc. of vs. 4 immediately above, the sense of this vs. – which seems surprisingly clear – is hard to square with our usual notions of Rigvedic reciprocal responsibilities, for the vs. states that Indra can kill all your relatives and still demand your offerings, with no attempt even to deny or distance himself from what he did. Geldner and Oldenberg pass over this unsettling doctrine in silence; Witzel Got┼Н suggest that the vs. shows that Indra doesnтАЩt fear a blood feud (Blutrache), but this seems to let Indra off too easily. There is no sign of the reciprocity that тАЬblood feudтАЭ implies: the hapless man whose relatives have been slaughtered does not seem to have done anything injurious to Indra, nor did his dead relatives – at least as far as the vs. allows us to see. The killings appear to be the arbitrary acts of a powerful god just because he can. It may be no accident that Indra is called ┼Ыakr├б- тАШableтАЩ here and in 3cd, where he also arbitrarily exerted his power.

(Of course, ┼Ыakr├б- is a common epithet of Indra in the RV and later, and I would not suggest that it is always used with this nuance – only that our poet exploited the literal sense of the word.) The fact that the word k├нlbiс╣гa- is used of IndraтАЩs deed supports the view that what he did was simply wrong; see published introduction.

I take pr├бyata- in its usual sense, referring to offerings or bounties тАШheld forthтАЩ or тАШpresentedтАЩ. Cf. nearby V.30.12 pr├бyat─Б magh─Б╠Бni, X.15.12 pr├бyat─Б hav─л╠Бс╣Гс╣гi, etc. I cannot get anything else out of this sentence than that Indra still wants the aggrieved man to keep making giving him oblations. Witzel Got┼Н tr. тАЬDarreichungen,тАЭ but suggest in their n. that it refers to тАЬReparations-, Satisfaktionszahlungen.тАЭ But what right would Indra have to seek reparations when he was the one who inflicted the damage? yataс╣Гkar├б- is a hapax, and the identity of neither of its parts is as sure as the standard interpr. take them. Grassmann suggests yataс╣Г belongs to the ppl. of тИЪyam, therefore morphologically identical to the immediately preceding (pr├б-)yat─Б, but this analysis is rejected, rightly in my view, by Geldner and Witzel Got┼Н, who take it (the former implicitly, the latter explicitly) as the acc. sg. of a root noun to тИЪyat, found also in the cmpd saс╣Гy├бt- in 9c. Although the uncompounded root noun is not found elsewhere and it is not mentioned by Schindler in his Root Noun diss. or Scarlatta in his disc. of тИЪyat (403-4), I think this must be the correct analysis, with the noun meaning тАШ(proper) arrangementтАЩ or the like. The published translation тАШarrangerтАЩ reflects this analysis of yataс╣Г, while taking 2nd member -kar├б- from тИЪkс╣Ы, hence тАШmake arrangementsтАЩ ├а тАШarrangerтАЩ. I now think this interpr. of the 2nd member is wrong. This p─Бda-final compound matches final ─Бkar├бс╕е of the next p─Бda, which, construed with preceding v├бsvaс╕е, means тАШdistributor of goodsтАЩ. This -kar├б- does not belong to тИЪkс╣Ы, however, but to тИЪkс╣Э, kir тАШscatterтАЩ, which occurs with ─Б╠Бin just this phrase: cf. IX.81.3 ─Б╠Бnaс╕е тАж kir─Б v├бsu тАЬscatter/distribute goods to us.тАЭ This strongly suggests that the parallel cmpd yataс╣Гkar├б- contains the same form, which leads to a sense тАШscattering the arrangementтАЩ – viz., destroying it, blowing it to smithereens and scattering the resulting particles. This accurately reflects what Indra has done in this vs. – violating the arrangement between men and gods – worship and offerings in return for protection, aid, and material goods – by smiting the family of his devotee, though he still provides goods. I would therefore change the published translation from тАШthe arrangerтАЩ to тАШscattering/destroying the arrangementтАЩ.

Griffith

The Strong God doth not flee away from him whose sire, whose mother or whose brother he hath done to death.
He, the Avenger, seeketh this man’s offered gifts: this God, the source of riches, doth not flee from sin.

Geldner

Der M├дchtige geht dem nicht aus dem Wege, dessen Vater, dessen Mutter, dessen Bruder er erschlagen hat. Er fordert sogar noch Geschenke von ihm, wenn er einen Vergleich macht. Er scheut vor keinem Unrecht zur├╝ck, der Verschenker des Gutes.

Grassmann

Wem Vater, Mutter oder Bruder er erschlug, vor dem auch weicht der starke nimmermehr zur├╝ck; Was man ihm darreicht, das nimmt der Bezwinger an, nicht weicht er der Gewaltthat, wenn er Gut verleiht.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬHe desires not (association in) enterprises with five or with ten; he associates not with the man who does not present libations; and cherishes not (his dependents) may, the terrifier (of foes) punishes him or slays him, but he plural ces the devout man in a pasturage stocked with cattle.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

He does not wish to grasp (the offerings) (only) by fives or tens. He does not keep company with a man who doesnтАЩt press (soma), even a prosperous one.
He either despoils (him as he goes) along the way, or the tumultuous one smashes (him). But he gives to the god-seeker a share in the pen full of cattle.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The usual arrangement beween Indra and mortals is re-established in this vs., where IndraтАЩs punishment comes only to the stingy and the non-worshipper, and the pious man gets rewarded.

There is a difference of opinion about the sense of p─Бda a, because of different interpr. of the acc. inf. ─Бr├бbham and of the numerical expressions. Geldner takes ─Бr├бbham as тАШsich verbindenтАЩ and the expressions of numbers as referring to people or gods – the sense being that Indra doesnтАЩt want to team up with others because heтАЩs strong enough on his own. But ─Б╠БтИЪrabh does not have that meaning, but only тАШto grasp, grab hold ofтАЩ. Witzel Got┼Н also take the numbers as personal: тАЬNicht w├╝nscht er mit f├╝nf, mit zehn (Leuten) das Erraffen (von Beute),тАЭ which I confess I donтАЩt understand. Is the intent that he wants to pile up his booty all by himself? By contrast, I take the numbers as referring to the means of grasping the offerings/goods – either by the number of gifts (=in increments of five or ten) or by handfuls: one (=five fingers) or two (=ten fingers) – and he doesnтАЩt want to acquire the goods in such trifling installments.

In c the question is the function of amuy─Б╠Б. I cannot identify a part of the Witzel Got┼Н tr. that represents amuy─Б╠Б. GeldnerтАЩs interpr. is minimalistic: ├нd amuy─Б╠БтАЬnur so,тАЭ which Klein (II.160) helpfully expands to тАЬonly in that circumstance (viz. when a wealthy person does not have soma pressed for him).тАЭ This may well be right. However, I compare X.135.2 c├бrantam p─Бp├бy─Бmuy─Б╠БтАЬgoing along yonder evil way.тАЭ In our passage this may refer to highway robbery: the offending non-presser gets robbed as he makes his way along the road. Or it may be metaphorical: if the non-presser continues to pursue this behavior heтАЩll be punished.

Griffith

He seeks no enterprise with five or ten to aid, nor stays with him who pours no juice though prospering well.
The Shaker conquers or slays in this way or that, and to the pious gives a stable full of kine.

рд╕рдореГрддреМ рд╕рдВрдЧреНрд░рд╛рдореЗ рд╡рд┐рддреНрд╡рдХреНрд╖рдгрдГ рд╡рд┐рд╢реЗрд╖реЗрдг рддрдиреВрдХрд░реНрддрд╛ рд╢рддреНрд░реВрдгрд╛рдВ рддрджрд░реНрдердВ рдЪрдХреНрд░рдорд╛рд╕рдЬрдГ рд░рдердЪрдХреНрд░рд╕реНрдпрд╛рд╕рдВрдЬрдпрд┐рддрд╛ рдЕрд╕реБрдиреНрд╡рддрдГ рдЕрдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирд╕реНрдп рд╡рд┐рд╖реБрдгрдГ рдкрд░рд╛рдЩреНрдореБрдЦрдГ рд╕реБрдиреНрд╡рддрдГ рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирд╕реНрдп рд╡реГрдзрдГ рд╡рд░реНрдзрдпрд┐рддрд╛ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдГ рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╕реНрдп рджрдорд┐рддрд╛ рд╢рд┐рдХреНрд╖рдпрд┐рддрд╛ рд╡рд┐рднреАрд╖рдгрдГ рднрдпрдЬрдирдХрдГ рдЖрд░реНрдпрдГ рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рдореА рдпрдерд╛рд╡рд╢рдВ рдпрдереЗрдЪреНрдЫрдВ рджрд╛рд╕рдВ рджрд╛рд╕рдХрд░реНрдорд╛рдгрдВ рдЬрдирдВ рдирдпрддрд┐ рд╕реНрд╡рд╡рд╢рдореН рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThinning (his enemies) in battle, and accelerating the wheels (of his car), he turns away from him who offers no libation, and augments (the prosperity of) the offerer; Indra, the subduer of all, the formidable, the lord, conducts the D─Бsa at his plural asure.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Very energetic in the clash, affixing the wheel (to the chariot?), he is antagonistic to the non-presser, but strengthener of the presser. Indra is the dominator of all, spreading fear; the ─Аrya leads the D─Бsa as he wishes.

Jamison Brereton Notes

There is puzzling agreement about the meaning of the hapax cakram─Бsaj├б-.

The standard interpr. run counter to the clear structure of the cmpd: a tatpuruс╣гa with the first member the acc. sg. of cakr├б- тАШwheelтАЩ (the acc. blocking hiatus before a vocalic 2nd member) and the 2nd derived from ─Б╠БтИЪsa(├▒)j. The lexeme ─Б╠БтИЪsa(├▒)j means тАШattach, affix, hangтАЩ (I.191.10, X.124.7); yet this cmpd is universally interpr. as meaning тАШimpeding/stopping the wheelтАЩ (Grassmann, Geldner, AiG II.1.183, EWA s.v. SA├СJ) or, acdg. to Witzel Got┼Н, тАШdie Wagen bremsendтАЩ with cakra- as pars pro toto. I do not understand this consensus that the verbal portion should be given a meaning not found with the verb itself, particularly since the context does not impose it. (S─Бyaс╣Зa.тАЩs gloss rathacakrasy─Бsa├▒jayit─Б does not seem to be responsible for it either.) Only Witzel Got┼Н attempt to trace a semantic pathway to the meaning attributed to ─Бsaj├б-, but it is not persuasive. I suppose all these interpr. are thinking of the myth in which Indra tears the wheel off the sunтАЩs chariot, but there is no other indication in context that this myth is at issue – and tearing off and stopping are quite different actions. Given these objections, I prefer to stick with the standard meaning of ─Б╠БтИЪsa(├▒)j and assume 1) that it refers to the restoration of the sunтАЩs wheel mentioned in regard to Eta┼Ыa in nearby V.31.11, or 2) that is refers to an incident in an unknown story, or 3) that it refers to some pre-batttle preparation or battle tactic. I prefer the first.

Griffith

Exceeding strong in war he stays the chariot wheel, and, hating him who pours not, prospers him who pours.
Indra the terrible, tamer of every man, as Arya leads away the Dasa at his will.

Geldner

Kraftvoll im Kampfe, das Rad aufhaltend, des Nichtpressers Widersacher, der St├дrker des Pressenden, eines jeden schreckbringender Bezwinger f├╝hrt Indra, der Arier, den Dasa, wie er will.

Grassmann

Der sehr gewalt’ge, der im Kampfe hemmt das Rad, ist feind dem, der nicht presst, dem Presser hold, Des Alls Bezwinger, Indra, der in Schrecken setzt; Barbaren f├╝hrt, wohin er will, der Arier.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬHe proceeds to plural nder the wealth of the (avaricious), and bestows the riches that are prized by man upon the donor (of the libation); every man is involved in great difficulty who provokes the might of Indra to wrath.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

He drives together the sustenance of the niggard, to steal it, but he shares out liberal goods to the pious.
In a (place) of no exit there is held firmly each and every people that has antagonized his power.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The lexeme s├бm тИЪaj is used elsewhere of тАШdriving togetherтАЩ cattle (I.33.3); here the bh├│janam of the niggard is presumably livestock. Though paс╣З├йс╕е here is used oppositionally to d─Б┼Ы├║с╣гe in b (see GeldnerтАЩs n. 7ab), the word also summons up IndraтАЩs opponents, the Paс╣Зis, who stole his cows – so stealing them back (muс╣г├й) is only justice.

The syntax of c is quite challenging. Let us begin with v├н┼Ыva ─Б╠Бpur├║. The phrase pur├║ v├н┼Ыva- appears to be an idiom, or at least is found twice in the RV, meaning тАЬall the manyтАЭ: I.191.9 pur├║ v├н┼Ыv─Бni тАЬall the many (bugs),тАЭ VII.62.1 pur├║ v├н┼Ыv─Б j├бnima тАЬall the many tribes.тАЭ Here, however, the words are in opposite order, with the preverb/adposition ─Б╠Бintervening, and the referent is singular (v├н┼Ыva[с╕е] тАж j├бnaс╕е). Nonetheless, I think the locutions are essentially the same, though I tr. тАЬeach and everyтАЭ to capture the singular number.

I do not know what to do with ─Б╠Б. It is possible that it is a preverb with dhriyate, but 1) though ─Б╠Бis found with тИЪdhс╣Ы, it is not common, and 2) preverbs in tmesis generally move to metrical or syntactic boundaries, and ─Б╠Бis not so placed here. The standard interpr. do not comment on it. I have no solution.

The last issue is the use of can├б. Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н) take it as neg. тАШnicht einmalтАЩ (not even). The sense of the clause, acdg. to them, is that a people that has provoked IndraтАЩs anger canтАЩt hole up for a long time even in a place thatтАЩs hard to penetrate.

Thus by their interpr. durg├б- is a desirable, fortress-like location for the offending people, but they canтАЩt hold onto it. But durg├б- is always otherwise an undesirable place, where no one wants to be – where we wish Indra to send our enemies (VII.25.2) but from which we want to be rescued. I therefore think that the point of this clause is that IndraтАЩs antagonists get confined to such a place and therefore can├б does not have a negative sense here. Twice loc. durg├й is followed by cid тАШevenтАЩ (VIII.27.18, 93.10), and durg├й can├б here may be a variant of this usage. Although he unfortunately does not discuss this passage, KleinтАЩs general disc. of can├б (DGRV I.285-92) as essentially borrowing negative value from the negative contexts in which itтАЩs ordinarily found allows for an original underlying positive value тАШevenтАЩ.

The published translation should be slightly altered to тАЬEven in a (place) тАж,тАЭ though IтАЩm not sure what sense тАШevenтАЩ adds – perhaps that not only are the people confined but they are confined in a really nasty place.

Griffith

He gathers up for plunder all the niggardтАЩs gear: excellent wealth he gives to him who offers gifts.
Not even in wide stronghold may all the folk stand firm who have provoked to anger his surpassing might.

Geldner

Er treibt den Wohlstand des Geizigen zusammen, um ihn zu rauben, und teilt dem Opferwilligen herrliches Gut zu. Nicht einmal in einer Bergfeste h├дlt sich sogar ein ganzer Volksstamm lange, der seine St├дrke gereizt hat.

Grassmann

Des Geiz’gen Nahrung nimmt zum Raube er hinweg, und dem Verehrer theilt er aus das reiche Gut; An festverschlossnem Ort auch h├дlt nicht lange Stand der Mann, der je des Indra Kraft zum Zorne reizt.

Elizarenkova

рд╕рдореН рдЕрд╡реЗрддреН рд╕рдВрдЬрд╛рдирд╛рддрд┐ рдпрддреН рдпрджрд╛ рдЬрдиреМ рдкрд░рд╕реНрдкрд░рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рджреНрд╡рдиреНрджреНрд╡рд┐рдиреМ рд╕реБрдзрдиреМ рд╢реЛрднрдирдзрдиреМ рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╢рд░реНрдзрд╕реМ рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдкреНрддрдмрд▓реМ рдмрд╣реВрддреНрд╕рд╛рд╣реМ рд╡рд╛ рдордШрд╡рд╛ рдзрдирд╡рд╛рдиреН рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдГ рдЧреЛрд╖реБ рд╢реБрднреНрд░рд┐рд╖реБ рд╢реЛрднрдирд╛рд╕реБ рдЧреЛрд╖реБ рдирд┐рдорд┐рддреНрддрднреВрддрд╛рд╕реБ рдЕрдиреНрдпрдВ рдпрд╖реНрдЯрд╛рд░рдВ рдпреБрдЬрдВ рд╕рд╣рд╛рдпрдореН рдЕрдХреГрдд рдХреГрддрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдкреНрд░рд╡реЗрдкрдиреА рд╢рддреНрд░реВрдгрд╛рдВ рдкреНрд░рд╡реЗрдкрдирд╡рд╛рдиреН ред рдИрдореН рдЕрд╕реНрдореИ рдЧрд╡реНрдпрдВ рдЧреЛрд╕рдореВрд╣рдореН рдЙрддреН рд╕реГрдЬрддреЗ рд╕рддреНрд╡рднрд┐рдГ рдорд░реБрджреНрднрд┐рдГ рд╕рд╣ рдзреБрдирд┐рдГ рдореЗрдШрд╛рдирд╛рдВ рдХрдореНрдкрдпрд┐рддрд╛ ред рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░реЛ рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирдореН рдЕрдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирдВ рд╡рд╛ рдпрдВ рдЬрд╛рдирд╛рддрд┐ рдЧреЛрдирд┐рдорд┐рддреНрддрдВ рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рддреНрд╡рд╛ рдпрдЬреНрд╡рдиреЗ рдЧреЛрд╕рдореВрд╣рдВ рдкреНрд░рдпрдЪреНрдЫрддреАрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWhen Indra, the possessor of opulence, discriminates between two men, both wealthy, and exerting themselves (against each other) for the sake of valuable cattle, he takes one of them as his associate, causing (his adversaries) to tremble, and the agitator (of the clouds), together with the Maruts, bestows upon him herds of cattle.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

When the two wealthy peoples with all their troops (clashed) together, Indra the bounteous pursued (them) in the (battles for) resplendent cattle.
Since the shaker has made one of them his yokemate, he drives up for himself the bovine (wealth) (of the other)тАФthe tumultuous one along with his warriors.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The identity of the verb ├бvet in b is disputed. Grassmann takes it as an opt. to тИЪav тАШhelpтАЩ; Oldenberg rejects that analysis but suggests that either тИЪvid тАШknowтАЩ or тИЪv─л тАШpursueтАЩ is possible. Geldner and Witzel Got┼Н (see also Oberlies RdV I.535) opt for тИЪvid and take the rest of the ab as indirect discourse controlled by this verb (тАЬwhen he found out that тАжтАЭ).

This is possible, but I find it hard to integrate subordinate y├бd clause in ab (with plupf.) with the h├н cl. of c (with root aor.) and the main cl. of d (with pres. indic.). I find that the sequence of tense works better if ab is a separate unit, with subord. y├бd cl. in a and main clause in b (├бvet accented because p─Бda-initial). Then c is the causal grounds for the main cl. in d and expresses immed. past.

My analysis requires supplying a verb in p─Бda a, linked to the preverb s├бm (which by the other interpr. must be construed with тИЪvid, a combination not found with тАШknowтАЩ, though it is with тИЪvid тАШfindтАЩ). A good candidate for a verb to supply is given by s├бmс╣Ыti- тАШclashтАЩ in 6a, and verbal forms to this idiom (s├бm тИЪс╣Ы) are fairly common. Cf. VII.25.1 тАж y├бt sam├бranta s├йn─Бс╕е тАЬwhen armies clash together.тАЭ My analysis also depends on a different analysis of ├бvet, which I assign to тИЪv─л тАШpursueтАЩ.

Note v├йti opening 4c.

The def. any├бm тАШthe oneтАЩ in c, referring to one of the two opponents in ab, more or less demands a responsive тАШthe otherтАЩ, as Geldner and I supply in d.

Oldenberg questions the existence of the stem pravepan├нn-, suggesting that pravepan─л╠Бis an adverbial instr. to a pravepan─л╠Б- (fld. by Witzel Got┼Н). I donтАЩt see that a stem pravepan─л╠Б- is appreciably better than an -├нn-stem and follow the older analysis.

Griffith

When Indra Maghavan hath marked two wealthy men fighting for beauteous cows with all their followers,
He who stirs all things takes one as his close ally, and, Shaker, with his Heroes, sends the kine to him.

English translation:

тАЬI, Arya, Agni, praise ┼Ъatri, the son of Agnive┼Ыa, the bestower of thousands, a type for comparison; may the collected waters yield him abundance; may wealth and strength, and glory be upon him.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Agni: Indra is referred as identical with Agni; Agnive┼Ыa is a с╣Ыс╣гi, a son of Brahm─Б

Jamison Brereton

The thousand-winning ─Аgnive┼Ыi ┼Ъatri will I sing, the measure and the beacon for the stranger, o Agni.
For him the waters will swell continuously; in him let there be lordly power aggressive and ardent.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The sense of saс╣Гy├бt- тАШcontinuous(ly)тАЩ, root noun cmpd. to тИЪyat (see yataс╣Гin 4c and disc. there), must have developed from тАШtaking their places together, one after the otherтАЩ. For further disc. of the stem, see comm. ad IX.86.15.

Griffith

Agni! I laud the liberal Agnivesi, Satri the type and standard of the pious.
May the collected waters yield him plenty, and his be powerful and bright dominion.

Geldner

Den Tausendschenker Satri, des Agnivesa┬┤ Sohn will ich feiern, o Agni, das Vorbild und die Leuchte eines hohen Herrn. F├╝r ihn sollen die Gew├дsser ununterbrochen anschwellen, bei ihm soll die m├дchtige, furchtgebietende Herrschaft verbleiben.

Grassmann

Den ├Зatri preise ich, den Nachkommen des Agnive├зa, der tausend Gaben schenkt, o Agni, den h├╢chsten Heerf├╝hrer des treuen [Volkes]; ihm m├╢gen fort und fort die Wasser reich an Nahrung sein; bei ihm verbleibe ungest├╝me starke Herrschaft.

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЗрд╕ рдордиреНрддреНрд░ рдореЗрдВ рд╡рд╛рдЪрдХрд▓реБрдкреНрддреЛрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдЩреНрдХрд╛рд░ рд╣реИред рдЬреЛ рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛ рд╣реЛрдиреЗ рдХреА рдЗрдЪреНрдЫрд╛ рдХрд░реЗ рддреЛ рд╕рд░реНрд╡ рд╢рд╛рд╕реНрддреНрд░реЛрдВ рдореЗрдВ рдкреНрд░рд╡рд┐рд╖реНрдЯ рд╣реБрдИ рд╕реНрд╡рдЪреНрдЫ рдФрд░ рдЙрддреНрддрдо рдЧреБрдгреЛрдВ рд╕реЗ рдпреБрдХреНрдд рдмреБрджреНрдзрд┐ рдХреЛ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реЛрдХрд░ рдЬреИрд╕реЗ рдкрд┐рддреГрдЬрди рдкреБрддреНрд░реЛрдВ рдХрд╛ рдкрд╛рд▓рди рдХрд░рддреЗ рд╡реИрд╕реЗ рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдУрдВ рдХрд╛ рдкрд╛рд▓рди рдХрд░реЗ, рдРрд╕рд╛ рдХрд░рдиреЗ рдкрд░ рд╢реНрд░реЗрд╖реНрда рд░рд╛рдЬреНрдп рдмреЭреЗ реерепрее рдЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдореЗрдВ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдФрд░ рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛ рдХреЗ рдЧреБрдг рд╡рд░реНрдгрди рдХрд░рдиреЗ рд╕реЗ рдЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдХреЗ рдЕрд░реНрде рдХреА рдЗрд╕ рд╕реЗ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдХреЗ рдЕрд░реНрде рдХреЗ рд╕рд╛рде рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐ рдЬрд╛рдирдиреА рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗ рее рдпрд╣ рдЪреМрдВрддреАрд╕рд╡рд╛рдБ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдФрд░ рдЪреМрдерд╛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реБрдЖ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рдЕрдЧреНрдиреЗ рд░рд╛рдЬрдиреН ! рдЕрд░реНрдпрд╕реНрддреНрд╡рдВ рд╕рд╣рд╕реНрд░рд╕рд╛рдорд╛рдЧреНрдирд┐рд╡реЗрд╢рд┐рдВ рд╢рддреНрд░рд┐рдореБрдкрдорд╛рдВ рдХреЗрддреБрдВ рдЧреГрдгреАрд╖реЗ рддрд╕реНрдореИ рдд рдЖрдк рдЗрд╡ рд╕рдВрдпрддрдГ рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдГ рдкреАрдкрдпрдиреНрдд рддрд╕реНрдорд┐рдВрд╕реНрддреНрд╡рдпрд┐ рд░рд╛рдЬреНрдЮрд┐ рдЕрдорд╡рддреНрддреНрд╡реЗрд╖рдВ рдХреНрд╖рддреНрд░рдорд╕реНрддреБ реерепрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкреБрдирд╕реНрддрдореЗрд╡ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдорд╛рд╣ рее

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рд╕рд╣рд╕реНрд░рд╕рд╛рдореН) рдпрдГ рд╕рд╣рд╕реНрд░рд╛рдирд╕рдВрдЦреНрдпрд╛рддрд╛рдиреН рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреН рд╕рдирддрд┐ рд╡рд┐рднрдЬрддрд┐ рддрдореН (рдЖрдЧреНрдирд┐рд╡реЗрд╢рд┐рдореН) рдпреЛрд╜рдЧреНрдирд┐рдВ рдкреНрд░рд╡реЗрд╢рдпрддрд┐ рддрдореН (рдЧреГрдгреАрд╖реЗ) рд╕реНрддреМрд╖рд┐ (рд╢рддреНрд░рд┐рдореН) рджреБрдГрдЦрд╡рд┐рдЪреНрдЫреЗрджрдХрдореН (рдЕрдЧреНрдиреЗ) рдкрд╛рд╡рдХ рдЗрд╡ (рдЙрдкрдорд╛рдореН) рджреГрд╖реНрдЯрд╛рдиреНрддрдореН (рдХреЗрддреБрдореН) рдкреНрд░рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдореН (рдЕрд░реНрдпрдГ) рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рдореА (рддрд╕реНрдореИ) (рдЖрдкрдГ) рдЬрд▓рд╛рдиреАрд╡ рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдГ (рд╕рдВрдпрддрдГ) рд╕рдВрдпрдордпреБрдХреНрддрд╛рдГ (рдкреАрдкрдпрдиреНрдд) рддрд░реНрдкрдпрдиреНрддрд┐ (рддрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН) (рдХреНрд╖рддреНрд░рдореН) рдзрдирдВ рд░рд╛рдЬреНрдпрдВ рд╡рд╛ (рдЕрдорд╡рддреН) рдЧреГрд╣реЗрдг рддреБрд▓реНрдпрдореН (рддреНрд╡реЗрд╖рдореН) рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рдпреБрдХреНрддрдореН (рдЕрд╕реНрддреБ) реерепрее
